## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations (nonlinear dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The variables (x, v, t) with target dv_dt indicate a second-order oscillator written as a first-order system, where acceleration is determined by restoring forces (often nonlinear in x), damping (often nonlinear in v), and possibly time-dependent driving/parametric terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (linear restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * x (small-amplitude linear spring/mass)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (damped harmonic oscillator)
- Duffing (cubic stiffness) with damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening nonlinear spring)
- Quadratic stiffness nonlinearity: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x * Abs(x) - c2 * v (asymmetric or piecewise-like stiffness effects)
- Nonlinear damping (quadratic drag-like): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (velocity-squared dissipation)
- Nonlinear damping (cubic): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (higher-order dissipation at large speeds)
- Pendulum-type restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (large-angle oscillations; periodic restoring torque)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance, hysteresis)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-like): dv_dt = -c0 * (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) * x - c4 * v (time-varying stiffness/parametric resonance)
- Van der Pol-type self-excitation: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (negative damping at small |x|, limit cycle)
- Rayleigh-type self-excitation: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (velocity-dependent negative damping, limit cycle)
- State-coupled damping/stiffness: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * x * v (amplitude-dependent dissipation or coupling effects)
- Time-varying damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) * v (modulated dissipation; can induce complex transients)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator signature: dv_dt depends on x but not explicitly on t, and damping terms in v are absent (energy approximately conserved).
- Restoring force symmetry: odd dependence in x (e.g., -c*x, -c*x**3, -c*sin(k*x)) typically implies symmetric oscillations about x=0; even-in-x terms suggest asymmetry/bias.
- Damping structure: terms proportional to v (or odd in v) dissipate energy; stronger-than-linear damping often appears as v*Abs(v) or v**3 dominating at high speeds.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency: inclusion of x**3 (Duffing) or sin(k*x) leads to frequency shifting with oscillation amplitude (hardening/softening behavior).
- Self-oscillation/limit cycles: “negative damping at small amplitude but positive at large amplitude” often appears as (c - x**2)*v or (c - v**2)*v.
- External forcing identification: additive periodic terms like cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) in dv_dt indicate driven oscillations and resonance phenomena.
- Parametric resonance indicator: time-periodic modulation multiplying x (or v), e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x, suggests Mathieu-type instability regions.
- Piecewise/impact-like stiffness: presence of Abs(x) (e.g., x*Abs(x)) can approximate unilateral constraints or stiffness changes across x=0.
- Coupled state dissipation: mixed terms like x*v often represent geometry-dependent damping or nonlinear coupling between displacement and velocity.
